## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (deterministic rate laws / ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt with inputs time t and concentration A matches ordinary-differential-equation descriptions of reaction kinetics, where a rate law specifies how concentration changes over time as a function of current concentration and possibly explicit time-dependent driving (e.g., programmed temperature, illumination, feed).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption; surface-limited or saturated reagent supply)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate formation; constant feed/source term)
- First-order decay (mass-action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition, dilute-limit kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order behavior)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order identification from data)
- Mixed source + first-order sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (approach to steady state under constant production and linear loss)
- Mixed source + n-th order sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A**c2 (steady state with nonlinear consumption)
- Reversible (relaxation to equilibrium concentration): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (linear return toward equilibrium A = c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth limited by depletion/carrying capacity c1)
- Generalized autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A) (autocatalytic order c1 with limitation by finite capacity)
- Rational inhibition (self-inhibition/saturation in rate): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate saturates at high A due to inhibition or limited active sites)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (linearly changing environment affecting effective rate constant)
- Periodic forcing of rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * A (photochemical/operational cycling causing periodic rate modulation)
- Stretched-exponential (time-dependent deactivation encoded in rate): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t**c2) * A (catalyst deactivation or aging reduces effective first-order rate with time)
- Empirical time-dependent source plus decay: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * t) - c2 * A (transient feed/pulse input with concurrent linear removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Identify reaction order from log-slope: if dA_dt scales like A^n, then plotting log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) is approximately linear with slope n (supports forms -c*A, -c*A^2, -c*A^n).
- Approach-to-equilibrium behavior: sign(dA_dt) flips around a stable fixed point A*; a linear relaxation model uses dA_dt proportional to (A - A*).
- Steady-state under source/sink: if dynamics converge to a constant A*, include an additive source term plus a consumption term (c0 - c1*A or c0 - c1*A^n).
- Autocatalysis signature: rate initially small at low A but accelerates as A grows; captured by multiplicative A factors such as A*(c1-A) or A^m*(c1-A).
- Self-inhibition/saturation signature: |dA_dt| increases with A at low A but plateaus at high A; modeled by rational forms like A/(c1 + A) multiplying a baseline rate.
- External protocol/forcing: if residuals correlate with t even at fixed A, include explicit time dependence via k(t) multiplying A (e.g., (c0+c1*t)*A, exp(-c*t)*A, or sinusoidal modulation).
- Catalyst deactivation/aging: progressively slowing kinetics at similar A suggests a decaying k(t), often exponential or stretched-exponential in time multiplying the concentration-dependent term.
- Pulse/feed experiments: transient bumps in dA_dt vs t imply additive source terms that decay in time (e.g., c0*exp(-c1*t)) combined with removal proportional to A.

\[
0.9709294495916855\,A^{1/3}-0.24581249010242617\,A.

So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to exactly “(constant)\(\cdot A^{1/3}\) + (constant)\(\cdot A\)” with **no remaining \(t\)-dependence** and **no extra \(A\)-dependence** (constants-only terms must be zero).

### 1
\(A^{1/3}c0e^{c1 t}+Ac2+Ac3 t+c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(c6 t+c7)\).

### 2
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+c2+c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\).  
Set \(c2=0,\ c3=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1\). Choose \(c0, c1\) as above. **Matches.**

### 3
\(A^{1/3}c0e^{c1 t}+Ac2+c3 e^{c4 t}\sin(\cdot)+c7 e^{c8 t)\).  
Set \(c1=0\); set \(c3=0\); set \(c7=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac2\). **Matches.**

### 4
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+c2+c3\log(c4 e^{c5\sin(\cdot)}+1)\).  
Set \(c2=0,\ c3=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1\). **Matches.**

### 5
\(A^{1/3}c0e^{c1 t}+A^{c2}c3+c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(\cdot)\).  
Need an \(A\) term and an \(A^{1/3}\) term. Set \(c1=0\), set \(c4=0\). For middle term choose \(c2=1\) so it is \(Ac3\). Then expression \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac3\). Pick \(c0, c3\) accordingly. **Matches.**

### 6
\(A^{1/3}c0e^{c1 t}+Ac2+c3 t+c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(\cdot)+c8\).  
Set \(c1=0,\ c3=0,\ c4=0,\ c8=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac2\). **Matches.**

### 7
\(A^{1/3}c0e^{c1 t}+A^2c2+Ac3+c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(\cdot)\).  
Set \(c1=0,\ c2=0,\ c4=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac3\). **Matches.**

### 8
\(A^{1/3}c0e^{c1 t}+A\cdot A^{c2}c3+A^{c2}c4+c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(\cdot)\).  
Set \(c1=0,\ c5=0\). To avoid extra powers, set \(c3=0,\ c4=0\) leaving \(A^{1/3}c0\) only—missing the \(-0.2458A\) term. Alternatively try to make one of the \(A^{c2}\) terms equal \(A\): if \(c2=1\), then \(A\cdot A^{c2}=A^2\) (bad) and \(A^{c2}=A\) (good) but then you still also have the \(A^2\) term unless \(c3=0\). With \(c3=0\), you can get an \(A\) term from \(A^{c2}c4\) but then you have no \(A^{1/3}\) unless \(c0\neq 0\) (fine). So choose \(c2=1,\ c3=0,\ c4=-0.2458,\ c0=0.9709\). Then expression is \(A^{1/3}c0 + A c4\). **Matches.**

### 9
\(A^{1/3}c0e^{c1 t}+A c2 e^{c3 t^{c4}}+c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(\cdot)\).  
To remove \(t\): set \(c1=0\); set \(c3=0\) so \(e^{0}=1\); set \(c5=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac2\). **Matches.**

### 10
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+c2\sin(Ac3+c4)+c5\).

### 11

### 12

Contains \(A^2\), \(A^{c1}\), \(\exp(Ac6)\), etc.

### 18

### 19
\(A^{1/3}c0 + A\cdot A^{c1}c2 + Ac3 + A^{c1}c4 + c5\).

### 20
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+c2+c3 e^{c4 t}\log(c5|Ac6|+1)\).

### 21
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+ A c2/(A c3 e^{c4 t}+c5 e^{c4 t})+c6\).  
The fraction term depends on \(t\) unless \(c4=0\) or \(c2=0\). Set \(c2=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1\). **Matches.**

### 22
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+ A c2 e^{c3 t^{c4}}+c5\).  
Set \(c2=0,\ c5=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1\). **Matches.**

### 23
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+c2 e^{A c3}+c4\).  
Exponential in \(A\) must vanish: set \(c2=0\). Set \(c4=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1\). **Matches.**

### 24
\(A\cdot A^{c0}c1 + Ac2 + A^{c0}c3 + c4 + c5\log(Ac6+1)\).  
Log term must vanish: \(c5=0\). Constant must vanish: \(c4=0\). Remaining has powers \(A^{c0}\) and \(A^{c0+1}\) plus \(A\). Hard to get exactly \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A\) simultaneously:  
- If \(c0=1/3\), you get \(A^{4/3}\) term unless \(c1=0\). Then you can keep \(A^{1/3}c3\) and \(Ac2\). Works with \(c1=0,\ c0=1/3,\ c3=0.9709,\ c2=-0.2458\). **Matches.**

### 25
\(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1+ A^{c2}c3/(A^{c2}+c4)+c5\).  
The rational term is not a pure power for all \(A\) unless removed: set \(c3=0\). Set \(c5=0\). Then \(A^{1/3}c0+Ac1\). **Matches.**
